--></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mrow>\n<mo>)</mo>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mtd>\n</mtr>\n<mtr>\n<mtd>\n<msub>\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<msub>\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<msup>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mi>i</mi>\n<mrow>\n<mo>(</mo>\n<mrow>\n<msub>\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mrow>\n<mo>)</mo>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mtd>\n<mtd>\n<msubsup>\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msubsup>\n</mtd>\n</mtr>\n</mtable>\n<mo>]</mo>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mo>&#10217;</mo>\n</mrow>\n</mtd>\n</mtr>\n</mtable>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\begin{aligned}\\mathbf {\\Psi } &amp;=\\left\\langle \\mathbf {e} \\mathbf {e} ^{\\dagger }\\right\\rangle \\\\&amp;=\\left\\langle {\\begin{bmatrix}e_{1}e_{1}^{*}&amp;e_{1}e_{2}^{*}\\\\e_{2}e_{1}^{*}&amp;e_{2}e_{2}^{*}\\end{bmatrix}}\\right\\rangle \\\\&amp;=\\left\\langle {\\begin{bmatrix}a_{1}^{2}&amp;a_{1}a_{2}e^{i\\left(\\theta _{1}-\\theta _{2}\\right)}\\\\a_{1}a_{2}e^{-i\\left(\\theta _{1}-\\theta _{2}\\right)}&amp;a_{2}^{2}\\end{bmatrix}}\\right\\rangle \\end{aligned}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle {\\begin{aligned}\\mathbf {\\Psi } &amp;=\\left\\langle \\mathbf {e} \\mathbf {e} ^{\\dagger }\\right\\rangle \\\\&amp;=\\left\\langle {\\begin{bmatrix}e_{1}e_{1}^{*}&amp;e_{1}e_{2}^{*}\\\\e_{2}e_{1}^{*}&amp;e_{2}e_{2}^{*}\\end{bmatrix}}\\right\\rangle \\\\&amp;=\\left\\langle {\\begin{bmatrix}a_{1}^{2}&amp;a_{1}a_{2}e^{i\\left(\\theta _{1}-\\theta _{2}\\right)}\\\\a_{1}a_{2}e^{-i\\left(\\theta _{1}-\\theta _{2}\\right)}&amp;a_{2}^{2}\\end{bmatrix}}\\right\\rangle \\end{aligned}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d870fffe2b96e063005e1456ecec66bd183ab4d5" style="vertical-align: -8.338ex; width:41.166ex; height:17.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where angular brackets denote averaging over many wave cycles. Several variants of the coherency matrix have been proposed: the <a href="/wiki/Norbert_Wiener" title="Norbert Wiener">Wiener</a> coherency matrix and the spectral coherency matrix of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Richard_Barakat&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Richard Barakat (page does not exist)">Richard Barakat</a> measure the coherence of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spectral_decomposition" title="Spectral decomposition">spectral decomposition</a> of the signal, while the <a href="/wiki/Emil_Wolf" title="Emil Wolf">Wolf</a> coherency matrix averages over all time/frequencies.\n</p><p>The coherency matrix contains all second order statistical information about the polarization. This matrix can be decomposed into the sum of two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Idempotent" title="Idempotent">idempotent</a> matrices, corresponding to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eigenvector" title="Eigenvector">eigenvectors</a> of the coherency matrix, each representing a polarization state that is orthogonal to the other. An alternative decomposition is into completely polarized (zero determinant) and unpolarized (scaled identity matrix) components. In either case, the operation of summing the components corresponds to the incoherent superposition of waves from the two components. The latter case gives rise to the concept of the "degree of polarization"; i.e., the fraction of the total intensity contributed by the completely polarized component.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Stokes_parameters">Stokes parameters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Polarization_(waves)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Stokes parameters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Stokes_parameters" title="Stokes parameters">Stokes parameters</a></div>\n<p>The coherency matrix is not easy to visualize, and it is therefore common to describe incoherent or partially polarized radiation in terms of its total intensity (<i>I</i>), (fractional) degree of polarization (<i>p</i>), and the shape parameters of the polarization ellipse. An alternative and mathematically convenient description is given by the <a href="/wiki/Stokes_parameters" title="Stokes parameters">Stokes parameters</a>, introduced by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_Gabriel_Stokes" title="George Gabriel Stokes">George Gabriel Stokes</a> in 1852. The relationship of the Stokes parameters to intensity and polarization ellipse parameters is shown in the equations and figure below.\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle S_{0}=I\\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>S</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>I</mi>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle S_{0}=I\\,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="S_0 = I \\," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0e4e4a14fdb0e907c33bba4272a9f4b2e731a514" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:7.136ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span></dd>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle S_{1}=Ip\\cos 2\\psi \\cos 2\\chi \\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>S</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>I</mi>\n<mi>p</mi>\n<mi>cos</mi>\n<mo>&#8289;<!-- &#8289; --></mo>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mi>&#968;<!-- &#968; --></mi>\n<mi>cos</mi>\n<mo>&#8289;<!-- &#8289; --></mo>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mi>&#967;<!-- &#967; --></mi>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle S_{1}=Ip\\cos 2\\psi \\cos 2\\chi \\,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle S_{1}=Ip\\cos 2\\psi \\cos 2\\chi \\,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8eecd37b64e27baa4f3acaf5592ab2aa2c3d92f4" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:21.37ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span></dd>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle S_{2}=Ip\\sin 2\\psi \\cos 2\\chi \\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>S</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>I</mi>\n<mi>p</mi>\n<mi>sin</mi>\n<mo>&#8289;<!-- &#8289; --></mo>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mi>&#968;<!-- &#968; --></mi>\n<mi>cos</mi>\n<mo>&#8289;<!-- &#8289; --></mo>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mi>&#967;<!-- &#967; --></mi>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle S_{2}=Ip\\sin 2\\psi \\cos 2\\chi \\,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle S_{2}=Ip\\sin 2\\psi \\cos 2\\chi \\,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/89654808fa9cfa7a564d577d05bcd87ec757288d" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:21.114ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span></dd>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle S_{3}=Ip\\sin 2\\chi \\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>S</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>3</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>I</mi>\n<mi>p</mi>\n<mi>sin</mi>\n<mo>&#8289;<!-- &#8289; --></mo>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mi>&#967;<!-- &#967; --></mi>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle S_{3}=Ip\\sin 2\\chi \\,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle S_{3}=Ip\\sin 2\\chi \\,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2121cc7652e619ee88835266f5953ffc88642baf" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:14.553ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>Here <i>Ip</i>, 2&#968; and 2&#967; are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spherical_coordinates" title="Spherical coordinates">spherical coordinates</a> of the polarization state in the three-dimensional space of the last three Stokes parameters. Note the factors of two before &#968; and &#967; corresponding respectively to the facts that any polarization ellipse is indistinguishable from one rotated by 180&#176;, or one with the semi-axis lengths swapped accompanied by a 90&#176; rotation. The Stokes parameters are sometimes denoted <i>I</i>, <i>Q</i>, <i>U</i> and <i>V</i>.\n</p>\n<h5><span id="Poincar.C3.A9_sphere"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Poincar&#233;_sphere">Poincar&#233; sphere</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Polarization_(waves)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Poincar&#233; sphere">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p>Neglecting the first Stokes parameter <i>S</i><sub>0</sub> (or <i>I</i>), the three other Stokes parameters can be plotted directly in three-dimensional Cartesian coordinates. For a given power in the polarized component given by\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msubsup>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle P={\\sqrt {S_{1}^{2}+S_{2}^{2}+S_{3}^{2}}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle P={\\sqrt {S_{1}^{2}+S_{2}^{2}+S_{3}^{2}}}}" aria-hidden="true" height:4.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>the set of all polarization states are then mapped to points on the surface of the so-called <i>Poincar&#233; sphere</i> (but of radius <i>P</i>), as shown in the accompanying diagram.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Poincar%C3%A9_sphere.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" <i>S</i><sub>3</sub>] (or [<i>Q</i>,&#8239;<i>U</i>,&#8239;<i>V</i>]) are plotted in Cartesian coordinates</div></div></div>\n<p>Often the total beam power is not of interest, in which case a normalized Stokes vector is used by dividing the Stokes vector by the total intensity <i>S</i><sub>0</sub>: \n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline normalized Stokes vector <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {S\'} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msup>\n<mi (<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle S\'_{0}=1}" significant Stokes parameters plotted in three dimensions will lie on the unity-radius Poincar&#233; sphere for pure polarization states (where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle P\'_{0}=1}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mrow>\n<mo>&#8242;</mo>\n</msubsup>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle P\'_{0}=1}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle P\'_{0}=1}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"
